Finance, Social Affairs, and Land Bureaus Issue Notice on Tax Reduction and Exemption 121

Setting Standards Based on Specific Circumstances

Complete Exemption for Jiangwan and Wusong

The Finance, Social Affairs, and Land Bureaus of this city, upon receiving an order from the Municipal Government yesterday, jointly issued a notice on the reduction and exemption of agricultural taxes in disaster areas within this city. The content includes: (1) Disaster areas in this city should have their agricultural taxes reduced according to the severity of the disaster. (2) Jiangwan and Wusong districts, which suffered the most severe disasters, are completely exempt from all agricultural taxes for the 21st year of the Republic. Yinhang and Zhenru districts will have their agricultural taxes reduced by 60%, Yinxiang and Pengpu districts by 40%, Zhabei district by 30%, and Huhnan and Pusong districts by 20%. (3) The remaining amount of agricultural tax reduced in each district will be collected together when the winter tax is collected. (4) Arrears from previous years in each district will not be exempted. The above measures have been submitted by the Municipal Government to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Interior for review and record, and the collection offices of agricultural taxes in this city have been instructed to comply.

Huang Yuzhou, Tang Juwu, and others from the General Headquarters of the Liaodong People's Self-Defense Army, received front-line reports from Ning yesterday, which are summarized as follows: (1) On August 15th, two Japanese civil engineering supervisors working on the railway bridge between Ying'emen and Shuiliandong on the Shenhai Line were captured by our army's 600-man broadsword team. (2) At 5:00 PM on August 16th, a Japanese scout was fishing in the Taizi River east of Benxihu and was killed by the Self-Defense Army. (3) Also on the same day at night, more than 300 cavalrymen from our Self-Defense Army launched a large-scale attack from the Qianshan Station south of Anshan. After more than 30 minutes of fighting, the Japanese police team was unable to withstand the attack and retreated, urgently reporting to the Fengtian Japanese garrison team, which then engaged in a fierce battle for more than two hours. The enemy was unable to withstand the attack, and the newly appointed President Lin Man fled to Anshan Station. Our Liaodong Self-Defense Army then occupied Qianshan Station. In this battle, 37 Japanese police officers were killed, and the number of wounded is unknown. Our side suffered 8 casualties, and obtained 25 rifles and more than 380 rounds of ammunition. (4) On the night of August 17th, more than 500 cavalrymen from our Self-Defense Army attacked between the Nantai Station and Tanggangzi on the main line of the South Manchuria Railway, cutting off all telegraph and telephone lines. The next day, they surrounded Nantai Station and attacked the Japanese garrison team, police team, and self-defense corps. The Haicheng and Anshan garrison teams provided field artillery support, and after six hours of fierce fighting, the enemy was unable to withstand the attack and retreated. Both sides suffered heavy losses in this battle. Our Self-Defense Army is still preparing to attack. (5) On August 18th, our Self-Defense Army is taking advantage of the obstruction of the green gauze tents, and is attacking the railway between Dashiqiao and Liaoyang at any time, destroying telegraphs and telephones, which are all out of service. The Japanese enemy is quite exhausted and struggling to cope. Further reports will follow.

Pan Yunchao's Speech on the Northeast Issue 124

Speech at the Chaozhou Fellow Association

The Chaozhou Shanghai Fellow Association and the Moral Education Group of the Four Virtues National Salvation Corps specially invited Mr. Pan Yunchao, a member of the Central Committee, to give a public lecture at the Fellow Association yesterday, which was held at 4:00 PM. More than 300 members attended. The meeting began with an introductory speech by Chairman Zheng Zhengqiu, who briefly stated: "Our group's Moral Education Group originally had lecture regulations, but due to the hot weather, we planned to hold them in the autumn. However, thinking of the Northeast volunteer army resisting the brutal Japanese army in this terrible summer, vowing to wash away the national humiliation with hot blood and fight for the lost land, we are in this difficult time for the country, and how dare we be afraid of the heat? Therefore, we are holding it early. Mr. Pan Yunchao's morality and articles are admired by our fellow villagers. This time, he was entrusted by Mr. Zhu Jiqing to preside over the rear affairs of the Northeast National Salvation Army. He must be deeply familiar with the situation in the Northeast, and our fellow villagers especially hope that he can tell us about the recent situation in the Northeast." Then, Mr. Pan Chaoyun gave a lecture (the long speech is recorded separately). Subsequently, Zheng Zhengqiu, Weng Ziguang, and others gave speeches with many words of encouragement. The meeting ended at around 6:00 PM. The following is Mr. Pan's speech:

Please, your association has enthusiastically helped me with the Northeast matters. Before I speak, I must express my gratitude. Today, I am honored to be invited by your association to give a lecture on the Northeast issue. With such a serious and complex Northeast, I know very little and cannot contribute much. I feel very sorry. Now, I will only briefly say that the Northeast incident is of great international importance. Japan, Soviet Russia, and even the United States are very complex. In a very short period of time, it is impossible to say everything. Now, let me first talk about Japan's conspiracy. Decades ago, Japan had an organization called the Black Dragon Society. The members of the society included politicians, soldiers, statesmen, and rogues. Its only principle was to invade China, not only in military and economic aspects, but also by adopting various methods and doing everything possible to invade. Taking advantage of the government's psychology and grasping the weaknesses of society, every civil war background must have Japanese people manipulating behind the scenes. Therefore, China has historically had many internal strife, politics is not on track, and society is so chaotic, directly and indirectly, all of which are affected by the Japanese. This time, we knew early on that their invasion and occupation of the Northeast was a consistent plan. Their entire proposition is to destroy China and even annex China. This is something that should be recognized first. Japan's invasion and occupation of the Northeast is not only for the Northeast, but also for the area north of the Yellow River, just like the previous invasion and occupation of Goryeo, the purpose is actually the Northeast in general. However, why did he not come out earlier? It is not because he is afraid of China, but because of international relations, afraid of offending the public. Now he sees clearly that the world economy is depressed, unable to take care of himself, and unanimously says that no country will unilaterally oppose Japan, and cannot unite to deal with it, while China is unable to resist, so he brazenly invaded at this time. This is something that should be recognized second. As for the origin of the Northeast Volunteer Army, it is not inherent, but because Japan occupied the Northeast, cut off and monopolized transportation, and divided it into many fragments. The Red Beard bandits in the Northeast are rampant everywhere, so the people have weapons at home for defense. Japan is not afraid of the Chinese government, but only of the people of the Northeast. He painstakingly wants to collect their weapons, which has caused a lot of resentment, because without weapons there is no guarantee, so they are greatly panicked and strive to resist. Furthermore, there are many enemies of the traitors, who often falsely report that a certain village has volunteer army firearms. The Japanese surrounded the village and killed old and young without mercy. The people felt that their own lives were in danger, and they became more united to seek self-defense. Therefore, before the establishment of the Volunteer Army and the National Salvation Army, there were countless times of scattered resistance. Because they are not the government's formal army, people call them the Volunteer Army. After the establishment of anti-Japanese groups in various places, they felt the pain of ununified command, so they united themselves. However, seeing the Volunteer Army representatives from Shanghai, claiming to be commanders-in-chief, there are already as many as seven people. Don't be pessimistic, this is a good phenomenon, because traffic is occupied, mountains are blocked, and the unity of each fragment is actually impossible. I am only afraid that the people will not rise up. As long as they rise up to resist, no matter if he is a commander or a commander-in-chief, it is always a good phenomenon. I am entrusted by Zhu Jiqing to handle the rear affairs of the Northeast National Salvation Army. Mr. Zhu is a person with a lot of history. He returned from studying in Japan in Xinhai and has been constantly running around for the revolution in his hometown of Liaoning. He has been active in the anti-Yuan protection law and other battles. He is a person who only knows how to do things and is not good at talking, so his name has never been prominent. This spring, he was living in Tianjin and, out of a sense of duty, was determined to go out of the pass to save the country. The volunteer army outside the pass also sent letters back and forth, inviting him to preside over the command. He went out of the pass with a serious illness, endured hardships, and did not avoid dangers. As a Central Committee member who was accustomed to living a privileged life, he ate cold water-soaked sorghum and walked six or seventy miles of mountain roads every day. It is naturally commendable. When he returned to Tianjin, I almost didn't recognize him. Haggard, dark, and skinny, he also had dysentery. But he was always very happy in his heart. He originally went to find a place to die, but now he is not only not dead, but also sees that he can do great things, so he is very excited to fight for a long time and goes around asking for help. The Northeast Volunteer Army has guns and blood, but what is lacking is insufficient ammunition. Although, they can also buy some from the Japanese and the traitors, but for the sake of the whole plan, it is still necessary to give thorough assistance. From the news of the Volunteer Army, we know the general situation of their work in the newspapers. It is indeed possible to do great things. Now there is a whole new plan, but I cannot announce it. In the near future, there may be very amazing and gratifying news that will spread to us. This is something to be comforted by everyone. Mr. Zhu is from the Northeast and is a subjugated slave. I am from Hebei and am a prepared subjugated slave. You may be the third or fourth candidate subjugated slaves. Japan's invasion of China is not a local issue, but a whole strategy. We must resist with all our strength. I hope everyone will rise up and work hard, work hard to help Mr. Zhu, work hard to help the subjugated slaves in the Northeast, and work hard to save the entire China that has not yet been subjugated.

Shanghai Customs Issues Notice on Revised Measures for Consular Invoiced 127

Tang Haian, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs and Acting Commissioner of Customs, issued a joint notice yesterday stating: "Regarding the implementation measures for the regulations on consular invoices issued by the consulates of the Republic of China abroad, a notice was issued on August 18th of this year. Now, we have received an order from the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance, stating that the original texts of Items A, B, and C listed in Article 9 of the said regulations should be cancelled immediately and revised as follows: A. For goods shipped from overseas during September and October of the 21st year of the Republic without consular invoices, the applicant should pay the customs the above-mentioned consular fee of five customs gold units, and the customs will reissue the consular invoice. B. For goods shipped from overseas during November and December of the 21st year of the Republic without consular invoices, the applicant should pay the customs twice the above-mentioned consular fee, totaling ten customs gold units, and the customs will reissue the consular invoice. C. For goods shipped from overseas on or after January 1st of the 22nd year of the Republic without consular invoices, the applicant should pay the customs a fine of fifteen customs gold units as stipulated in Article 9 of these regulations, and the customs will reissue the consular invoice. Comply with these instructions and handle accordingly. All merchants are hereby notified."

The Jiangnan Embankment Project Has Been Completed 129

The Rehabilitation Committee Prepares to Conclude

The Jiangnan Embankment Rehabilitation Committee sent letters yesterday to the Jiangsu Provincial Government, the Shanghai Municipal Government, and related agencies such as the Construction Department and the Public Works Department, stating: "Since the beginning of our committee's organization, after the end of the Shanghai war, both public and private sectors have been in difficulty, and fundraising has been difficult. However, the timing is pressing, and all surveys and designs have not been able to be carefully planned. The members have their own professions, and their energy has not been able to be concentrated. Over the past five months, we have been deeply concerned about failure. Fortunately, the government authorities are concerned about the people's livelihood and deeply understand the importance of embankment work. The huge allocation of funds is unprecedented since the Republic of China, and the employees are also able to understand the government's intentions, encourage diligence, and be impartial. The committee members rely on the assistance of the financial community and are also able to fulfill their responsibility of lending a hand to share the burden, so that the employees can work with peace of mind. Now, 80 to 90% of the completed projects will be completed as scheduled in mid-September. This is what the committee members can report to the government and local elders. However, the Jiangnan embankment has been in disrepair for a long time. The first survey by the committee members actually required 3 million yuan to complete the symptomatic treatment project. However, due to limited funds, the completed projects only account for a quarter of the original plan. The committee members have repeatedly visited the construction site for supervision and inspection, and the dangers are becoming more apparent. We deeply feel that the previous survey of the project was not exhaustive, and the current completed projects are too far from the actual situation. This year's tide season has passed more than half, and fortunately, no major dangerous projects have occurred. This is due to the tireless patrols of the employees, and the fact that the wind and tide have not been severe, which is the biggest reason. Looking ahead to next year, we have deep concerns. If the survey work cannot be completed uniformly in the years to come, and the annual maintenance costs cannot be guaranteed every year, then the residents of Songhu will always have the suffering of fainting and the danger of drowning. The committee members' meeting and organization are temporary. Now, as the completed projects are about to be completed, we should immediately prepare for the conclusion and have already reported it in another case. In the future, raising huge amounts of money and continuing to carry out major projects will make the embankment permanent and the people's livelihood secure. We can only rely on the government to supervise, and permanent institutions to make overall plans and take care of all aspects to comfort the people. All the projects that have not been surveyed and repaired by the committee are copied with a list and sent for inspection."

All Sectors in Shanghai West Organize Committee to Promote Dredging After Puhuitang's Siltation 130

Electing Ma Xiangbo and 12 Others as Committee Members

Puhuitang in Shanghai West is silted up, which hinders the people's livelihood and should be dredged urgently. The parks in the area specially invited the Song Qing Municipal Government and the gentry along the pond to discuss solutions. A meeting was held on August 22nd at Sanshantang to discuss. Shen Yi, Director of the Municipal Public Works Bureau (represented by Liu Yuecang), Fang Erkang, Director of the Qingpu County Construction Bureau, Xu Baikui, Director of the Songjiang County Construction Bureau (represented by Wu Zhaosheng), Hu Lifu of Fahua, Gu Rungui, Pan Boxian, Wang Shenyuan, Jiang Jusheng of Pusong, Yang Fuyuan of Caojing, Wu Yuqing, Li Wenlai of Sijing, Zhang Yande, and Zhang Weicheng, Shen Caigeng, etc., publicly elected Zhang Weicheng as the chairman. First, the chairman reported, followed by a report by the representative of the Municipal Public Works Bureau on the measurement process. The directors of the Qingpu Construction Bureau and the representatives of the Songjiang Construction Bureau successively reported, all saying that if the river water is so smelly, it is not enough to benefit the people's livelihood if the municipal government is not asked to dredge it at the same time. The chairman then read a letter from Mr. Ma Xiangbo, proposing to open a small gate from the west of Longhua Baibu Bridge to Jiuli'an, and a written opinion from Mr. Wang Dianxian. After discussion, it was decided that to avoid the smell, it is necessary to change the route. The proposal to change the route should be submitted to the municipal government for approval. A committee to promote the dredging of Puhuitang was established on the spot, and Ma Xiangbo, Yang Binghang, Chen Yafu, Yang Fuyuan, Zhang Weicheng, and other thirteen people were elected as members to request the municipal government to dredge it together to benefit farmers and merchants and to comfort the public.

At 7 PM the day before yesterday, Jardine Matheson's steamer "Tingsang" arrived in Shanghai from Tianjin, carrying 132 postal employees from the Northeast. The Shanghai Administration Director, Chapin, and the specially appointed Postal Commissioner, Wu Yu, braved the rain to welcome them at Jardine Matheson Wharf in Yangshupu. After disembarking, the postal employees were transported directly to the Jingwu Athletic Association's rest area in Fudeli, Yokohama Bridge, by postal delivery vehicles. At 12 PM yesterday, all employees went to the Shanghai Postal Administration on Sichuan Road Bridge to meet Postal Commissioner Chapin, specially appointed Postal Commissioner Wu Yu, and Deputy Postal Commissioner Wu. They also submitted a report. Chapin then reported to the General Administration, which had already assigned placement arrangements through the General Affairs Department. Eighty-six employees were assigned to Shanghai, and thirty-six were assigned to the General Administration. A reporter from the Datong News Agency visited the employees at the athletic association yesterday afternoon. According to them, most of them had entered the pass last month. They had been in Tianjin for two weeks and finally boarded a ship in Tanggu on the 19th of this month to come to Shanghai. All the employees' families are still in Tianjin. According to evening news, the employees assigned to work in Hangzhou have already received orders from the General Administration, instructing them to report to the Hangzhou office tomorrow morning (today) by taking the early train from the South Station.

Shen Bao, Section Six

Local News, Two

Son Posthumously Names Father a Traitorous Merchant 132

Mitsui Comprador Gu Zhenxian

Repeatedly Scorned and Cursed by His Son

Son Accused in Another Case

Court Discusses Father's Evil Deeds

Gu Chengyou, son of Gu Zhenxian, a comprador for the Japanese Mitsui & Co., has been deeply fearful that the country will be lost without end since the Japanese invaders occupied the Northeast and shelled Shanghai. He repeatedly advised his father not to cooperate with the Japanese anymore and to resign from his comprador position in time to avoid social scorn. However, Zhenxian stubbornly refused and remained loyal. His son then privately named him a traitorous merchant. Recently, he even sent a letter in the name of the Blood Soul Group, issuing a stern warning, hoping to make his father pull back from the brink. However, Zhenxian, being greedy for wealth and position, remained unmoved and even drove his son away. Chengyou was extremely angry, and his nerves were also disordered. On the 22nd, he suddenly went to Wing On Company on Nanjing Road South empty-handed and arbitrarily selected items worth 1,000 yuan. He asked the company to send someone to his home at 3 Xuanshou Lane, Jingxiu Road in the city, to collect the money. Upon arriving at the home, his stepmother refused to pay and ordered the deliveryman to go to Mitsui & Co. on Sichuan Road to ask his father for payment. Zhenxian was out at the time, so the deliveryman took the goods back. The next morning, Chengyou called Wing On Company, saying that he had prepared the money and urged them to deliver the goods quickly. When the company sent someone to his home again, no one paid. Wing On Company believed that this behavior was deceptive and reported it to the Laozha Police Station. Detective Ye Yushi arrested Gu Chengyou and took him to the police station. Gu then poured out to the police chief all the facts about his father willingly flattering the Japanese and wanting to be a traitorous merchant. Yesterday morning, the police station sent Gu to the First Special District Local Court. Judge Liu interrogated him. The police lawyer, Qian Xunjiu, accused the defendant of fraudulently obtaining property and requested punishment according to Article 363 of the Criminal Law. When questioned, the defendant stated that his mother had initially agreed to give him 700 yuan, so he went to buy things. The purchase only slightly exceeded the amount. He did not expect his mother to suddenly refuse to give him any money after the purchase. He also requested the court to give him fifteen minutes to fully describe the facts of his father being a traitorous merchant. The judge instructed him that matters unrelated to the case would not be tolerated. He then pronounced the verdict: Gu Chengyou was sentenced to three months imprisonment for the crime of attempted fraudulent acquisition of property. After hearing the verdict, Gu still muttered to himself, saying that if he had been allowed to state the facts briefly, he would have been willing to accept the punishment.

Account of the Qitai Steamer's Ordeal 133

Goods from Shashi Cease Transportation

Shashi is an important port in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. A large amount of miscellaneous grains are shipped out every year. Various steamer companies in Shanghai have all dispatched steamers to travel there. However, recently, due to the suppression of communists, panic has arisen. Goods from Shanghai to Shashi have completely stopped loading, and the Jiejiang's Qitai steamer even encountered a shock in Shashi. The details are recorded below.

Qitai Encountered Bandits

The Jiejiang's Qitai steamer, traveling from Shanghai to Yichang, encountered the Red Army under He Long's command about thirty miles downstream from Shashi on the 16th of this month. The bandits opened fire on the steamer, intending to rob it. A team of American soldiers stationed on the Qitai steamer immediately returned fire with machine guns. However, the Red Army was numerous, and the Qitai was in great danger. Fortunately, the Jincheng warship dispatched by the Sichuan Army arrived and drove the communists back, allowing the Qitai to escape danger and sail upstream.

Misunderstanding During Steamer Inspection

Shashi is currently garrisoned by Wang Fangzhou's troops. Regiment Commander Yang Hui is responsible for Shashi's security. When the Qitai steamer arrived at the mouth of Shashi, the garrison ordered it to stop for inspection to prevent communists from infiltrating. The shipowner, Tyler, said that the water was too rapid to dock and requested inspection at the pier. The garrison did not understand him and saw that the Qitai did not stop. They thought it was resisting orders and fired warning shots. The American soldiers inside the ship mistakenly thought it was a second attempt by the Red Army to rob the ship and used machine guns to fire at the garrison on the shore, resulting in a big misunderstanding. Later, a large team of garrison troops arrived and detained the Qitai.

Arrest of the Captain

The Shashi garrison troops boarded the Qitai steamer and arrested Captain Tyler and the ship's comprador to investigate who had opened fire. They demanded that the person be handed over, saying that four garrison soldiers had been injured by bullets. The American soldiers on the ship, knowing that they had caused the trouble due to a misunderstanding, hid in the cabin. The shipowner was brought to the headquarters and saw Regiment Commander Yang. The Chinese comprador explained that it was a misunderstanding and not a deliberate act of resisting the military inspection. The escorting American soldiers had encountered communists midway and acted in self-defense. He described the process of escaping the bandits. Regiment Commander Yang released Tyler after repeated proof from the crew.

Merchandise Shipped Out of Shashi

Due to the serious suppression of bandits, merchants in the city hired steamers to ship out all their stored merchandise to Hankou for storage. Banks also entrusted their stored cash to Jardine Matheson's Baohuo steamer for temporary storage in Hankou. Boxes and items from various merchants are also being loaded onto a hired steamer. If necessary, they can be shipped downstream. A prepared merchant steamer is also anchored in front of the Shashi Customs.

Suspension of Merchandise Business

Since the 15th and 16th of this month, Shashi merchants have completely stopped doing business. There are telegrams asking that the goods purchased in Shanghai not be shipped for the time being. The export of goods from Shanghai to Shashi has also stopped. As for the goods stored in the Shashi warehouses, they are being rushed to be shipped to various ports. They must be shipped out in a short period of time.

Robbers Who Are Also Kidnappers 134

Letters Demanding Ransom Arrive One After Another

Second-Hand Goods Vendor Apprehended by Guards

Qiao Guanxiang, a carpenter residing west of the Hongqiao Airport in Shanghai's western suburbs, near the Datie Bridge, has gradually become well-off through diligence and thrift. His wife, Jiang, has given birth to three sons: Shunyu, 16, Xiaoshun, 10, and a baby brother only a few months old. Recently, they were targeted by bandits. On the morning of the 11th of this month, at around 2 AM, eight bandits speaking a mixed dialect and wearing white short shirts and pants broke into the house. Four of them had pistols. They ransacked the chests and boxes and threatened and extorted silver dollars from Qiao Guanxiang, but failed. He was then hit on the left hand with an iron bar. His mother, Yao, and wife, Jiang, were also seriously injured by the bandits kicking them. A neighbor, Gu Yunting, went out to call for help and was shot by the bandits, with bullets piercing both legs. He is still being treated at the Red Cross Hospital on Route Haig and has not recovered. Seeing that there were no valuables, the bandits kidnapped Qiao's second son, Xiaoshun, and fled east. Afterward, the victim reported the incident to the Xu Jing Public Security Branch of Qingpu County and the Second Water Police Team, requesting a thorough investigation. However, the victim received two letters from the post office the day before yesterday. The first letter said, "Your son is currently being cared for and treated very well. There is no need to worry." The second letter demanded a ransom of 200 yuan, specifying that the victim should come to negotiate at the west of the railway on Hongqiao Road in the western suburbs of Shanghai between 2 PM and 4 PM on the 23rd of the lunar calendar (yesterday). The person coming would be identified by carrying a Great Britain brand listening device wrapped in red cloth and an umbrella. If there was no sincerity in negotiating, drastic measures would be taken. After receiving the letter, Qiao reported to the Public Security Branch and the Water Police Team. Inspector Luo Desheng and detectives Yao Youlian and others were dispatched in disguise. The Sixth District, First Branch, Hongqiao Road Police Station of the Municipal Public Security Bureau was also notified to assist. Until 5 PM, Song Wanjun and Ma Shifu, two Jiangbei Rugao natives selling second-hand goods, were seen wandering around at the intersection of Yangzhai Road and Hongqiao Road, repeatedly observing the victim. The detectives, seeing their suspicious behavior, stepped forward to arrest them and brought them, along with the second-hand goods pole, to the Sixth District, First Branch. After the station chief, Bi Zhenhua, presented the case for strict interrogation, Song and Ma vehemently denied the robbery, looting of money, kidnapping, and demanding ransom. Station chief Bi, believing the case to be serious, ordered them to be temporarily detained pending further investigation.

Jianghai Customs Uncovers Yongshou Huaxing's Smuggling of Tax-Evasion Jewelry and Diamonds 135

Worth Hundreds of Thousands

Shop Owner Qiu Yonghua Arrested

Assets Seized by Customs

Yongshou Huaxing, located on the fourth floor of the China Agricultural and Industrial Bank at the corner of Jiujiang Road and Henan Road, specialized in smuggling valuable items such as jewelry and diamonds into the country to evade taxes. After a long investigation by Jianghai Customs, solid evidence was finally obtained yesterday. The Central Police Station was notified to conduct a joint search. In addition to arresting the shop owner, Qiu Yonghua, at the shop around 10 AM, several Chinese and foreign associates were also arrested and handed over to the police station. After Jianghai Customs and the concession authorities inspected the shop's books, they discovered that many goods had been smuggled in to evade taxes. The value of the diamonds, jewelry, and ornaments reached hundreds of thousands. Jianghai Customs requested the Special District Court to order the police station to allow all assets in the shop to be moved to Jianghai Customs for further handling.

Further News on the Collision of Two British Steamers 136

Both Steamers Seriously Damaged

Losses Still Under Investigation

The Jardine Matheson North China liner Lishun collided with the Blue Funnel Line (Calchas) Koureksis at 1:15 PM the day before yesterday near Qichang Wharf while leaving port. The two steamers were damaged. The details are recorded below.

Details of the Incident

The Blue Funnel Line foreign steamer Koureksis, loaded with a large batch of gasoline and steel from London, as well as 1,700 tons of goods bound for Japan, arrived in Shanghai on the 19th and docked at the Blue Funnel Wharf in Pudong. After unloading the goods, it planned to leave for Japan at around 1 PM yesterday. While turning around to leave port and approaching the Qichang Wharf, it had just used a tugboat to pull the bow outward when the Jardine Matheson's Lishun steamer, also leaving port, approached from behind. Due to the rapid water and strong winds, it also hired a Hutchison tugboat to tow it. Although the Koureksis had turned around properly, the tide was rising and the water was rapid. The steamer was pushed backward by the tide. The Lishun steamer saw the steamer reversing and, although it reversed its engines, it was too close to avoid a collision.

Both Steamers Damaged

The rapid current and strong winds pushed the Koureksis backward, and the Lishun steamer could not avoid it. The bow of the Lishun struck the stern of the Koureksis. Because the Koureksis was large and high, the Lishun was small, so it struck below the stern deck of the Koureksis, directly at the propeller and rudder. Although the Lishun was damaged at the time, it was below the waterline. Only the copper railings on the bow were damaged, and the damage below was not noticed. It was still towed outward by the tugboat. Later, the tugboat gradually became overloaded and unable to tow. The small boat noticed that the bow of the Lishun was gradually sinking and notified the Lishun steamer. The shipowner, upon receiving the report, ordered someone to inspect the forepeak, which was already flooded. They used pumps to pump the water, but it was ineffective. They quickly sailed to a shallow beach and grounded the ship on the Lancun Beach in Yangshupu. They only knew that a hole had been punctured. At that time, the water was high and the wind was strong, so they first secured the steamer. They later learned that the starboard side had been severely damaged and reported it to the company. They also reported it to the Marine Department of the Customs. After the Koureksis collided with the Lishun, it also felt that the propeller was not working properly. It was later discovered that a propeller blade was damaged, so it stopped leaving port and was repaired in Shanghai.

Passengers and Cargo Transferred

The Lishun steamer was traveling from Shanghai to Weihai, Yantai, Tianjin, etc. It was loaded with more than 16,000 bags of flour, 600 bags of rice, more than 2,000 pieces of paper, more than 200 boxes of tea, and more than 800 pieces of miscellaneous goods, totaling about 1,500 tons. There were seven Western passengers and more than forty Chinese passengers. After the incident, they all disembarked. The cargo in the cabin, especially the forepeak, was already flooded. Today, barges were hired to completely transfer the cargo. It was also seen that there was a large hole in the starboard side of the forepeak, with a propeller blade still embedded in the iron plate. According to the company, after the cargo is transferred, it will be repaired at the Ruirong Shipyard today. The loss for repairs is estimated at more than 20,000 yuan. The loss of cargo will be investigated later.

Responsibility Assessment

After the incident, the Rivers and Harbors Department of the Customs received the report and sent personnel to the scene to investigate and inquire about the circumstances of the incident from the two shipowners for reference. As for the issue of responsibility, because both steamers were British-owned, it will be judged by the British Consulate General in Shanghai in the future. The two companies were very busy handling the ship repairs, so negotiations had not yet begun yesterday.

Regulations on the National Railway's Responsibility for Freight Transport (3) 138

(14) Losses caused by customs or tax bureau detention of goods; (15) Losses caused by war or mass riots; (16) Losses caused by legal sanctions; (17) Losses caused by the consignor's own vehicles due to poor equipment or improper repair; (18) Where the original packaging of goods is intact, but the contents are not of the correct quality, or the nature has changed, or there are shortages; (19) Where the consignor loads entire cars of goods on dedicated sidings, if the seal added by the consignor is intact, but the contents are short in number, weight, or the packaging is damaged and the goods are lost. Article 37: Cargo Fire Insurance. For goods transported by the railway, the railway may take out fire insurance with insurance companies. All matters shall be handled in accordance with the fire insurance regulations. The fire insurance fee shall be collected separately from the freight and miscellaneous fees. If the consignor does not take out fire insurance or seeks their own insurance, they may do so. If the consignor wishes to entrust the railway to take out fire insurance, they must indicate "Please take out fire insurance" in the special agreement column of the consignment note. For goods that are not entrusted to the railway for fire insurance, the consignor shall be responsible for any damage caused by fire. Article 38: Open Car Loading or Open-Air Storage of Goods. If goods are loaded in open cars or stored in the open air in the freight yard, the railway shall not be responsible for any loss or damage caused by strong winds, heavy rain, or other sudden changes in the weather that cannot be resisted by human power. Article 39: Consignor's Responsibility. If goods entrusted to the railway for transport cause damage to other people's goods or railway property due to self-ignition, improper packaging, or the consignor's or their caregiver's intentional or negligent acts, the consignor shall be liable for all damages. Consignors shall not move vehicles without the railway's permission when loading or unloading goods. At any time, if accidents or damage to vehicles and their accessories occur as a result, they shall be liable for compensation. Lighting lamps, smoking, or other dangerous acts are prohibited in the freight yards of each station. If accidents are caused by the consignor's or their employee's negligence, the consignor shall be fully responsible. When a consignor is liable for compensation to the railway or other damaged consignors, the compensation standard shall be based on the railway's existing regulations. If there are no regulations, it shall be estimated temporarily. Article 40: Goods for Which the Railway Is Not Responsible for Transport. The railway does not handle responsible transport for the following goods: (1) Goods for which freight is charged according to the sixth class of goods, unless specially permitted by the railway; (2) Goods transported at a special price, the freight rate of which is the same as or lower than the sixth class of goods; (3) Live poultry and livestock; (4) Empty boxes, empty buckets, empty bags, and empty packages with the words "Empty Items Returned" marked on the outside; (5) Explosives and dangerous goods listed in the Ordinary Goods Classification Table attached to the Freight Car Transport Regulations, except for kerosene, firecrackers, matches, film, oil, and other goods that have other regulations; (6) Coffins; (7) Gold, silver, gold and silver currency, banknotes, and valuable securities; (8) All important documents and valuable items listed or not listed in the Ordinary Goods Classification Table attached to the Freight Car Transport Regulations, but those specially permitted by the railway. (Chapter 6) Compensation for Losses. Article 41: Claims Procedures. If all or part of the goods are damaged or lost, (if the goods have not arrived at the destination station within one month from the date when they should have arrived, and the railway cannot determine the location of the goods, they shall also be treated as lost goods).

When the consignor claims compensation, the consignor shall make the claim before the goods are shipped. After the goods arrive at the destination station, the consignee shall make the claim. After the goods are shipped and before they arrive at the destination station, the consignor or the consignee shall make the claim. Whether the consignor or the consignee, before claiming compensation, must go to the site to jointly deal with the station chief to check the loss of the goods, and must indicate "damaged or lost several pieces and weight" on the responsible freight receipt or bill of lading, and then immediately or within the shortest time fill out a "Compensation Claim Form" prepared by the railway, together with the relevant documents (such as the price certificate of the goods, the receipt for the goods stored in the yard, the responsible freight receipt or bill of lading, and a detailed list of the goods), and submit them to the handling station chief. After receiving the claim form, the station chief must quickly forward it to the director of the Transportation Department for verification and handling, and issue a "Compensation Claim Form Receipt" to the claimant as proof for receiving compensation in the future. If compensation is claimed without following all of the above procedures, the railway may refuse to handle it. Article 42: Investigation and Compensation. When goods are lost or damaged and the consignor or consignee claims compensation, the railway shall promptly investigate and decide on the compensation matters immediately after all inquiries are completed. (1) If the railway finds the lost goods before the compensation is decided and sends the goods intact to the claimant or their representative for receipt, the railway shall be deemed to be relieved of its compensation responsibility. (2) If goods are lost or damaged, the railway may also consider the circumstances and compensate with goods of the same quality for the lost or damaged goods. (3) If goods are lost or damaged and the railway should pay compensation, the limit of the compensation price shall be based on the ordinary market price of the same goods at the time of consignment at the shipping station. The freight and miscellaneous fees already paid shall be refunded together. However, the market price shall not exceed the amount specified in the consignment note. If the value is specified in the consignment note, the actual price must still be proved by the claimant. As for the loss of part of the goods, the railway shall compensate the price of the goods and refund the freight and miscellaneous fees in proportion to the ratio of the lost part to the total goods. Article 43: Handling of Recovered Lost Goods After Compensation. If the railway recovers the lost goods after paying compensation, it shall immediately notify the claimant to return the compensation paid by the railway and pick up the goods. If no one picks up the goods one month after the notification is issued, the railway shall dispose of the goods itself. If the address is unknown and notification is impossible, the railway shall announce the recovered goods at the shipping station and the destination station for one month. If no one picks up the goods after the deadline, the railway may dispose of the goods itself. Article 44: Elimination of the Right to Claim Compensation. The right to claim compensation for losses of goods shall be eliminated after six months from the date of discovery of the loss, unless otherwise specified. (Chapter 7) Supplementary Provisions. Article 45: These Regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation. Article 46: After these Regulations are implemented on all lines, all previous regulations on freight car transport responsibility shall be repealed. Article 47: If there are any matters not covered in these Regulations, the Ministry of Railways may amend them at any time.

Now we have received Directive No. 2139 from the Executive Yuan, stating that the situation has been forwarded to the Legislative Yuan for prompt review and response. Reports on the Dutch Government's Exclusion of Apollo

Central Government Telegraphed Mayor Wu, Ordering Sanyou Factory to Resume Work Immediately 142

Before Resuming Work, Sufficient Food Supplies Must Be Provided

Families of Hunger-Striking Workers Came to Shanghai to Visit the Sick

Regarding the labor-capital dispute at the Sanyou Factory, the Central Government yesterday telegraphed the Municipal Party Committee, the Municipal Government, and Mayor Wu, ordering them to use extraordinary means to force the capitalists to resume work immediately. The hunger-striking workers were all sent to the Labor Hospital and Shanghai Hospital the day before yesterday, and their lives are generally out of danger. Details are as follows:

Central Government Ordered Factory to Open The Mass Movement Guidance Committee of the Central Party Headquarters telegraphed the Municipal Party Committee and the Municipal Government yesterday, saying: "Mayor Wu of the Municipal Party Committee and the Municipal Government, the Sanyou Industrial Company has been delayed in resuming work, and the workers are on hunger strike, which is a very tragic situation. Please use extraordinary means to force the capitalists to resume work immediately. Before resuming work, sufficient food supplies must be provided for the workers. Please convey this. The Mass Movement Guidance Committee of the Central Government salutes you."

Current Situation of Hunger-Striking Workers A total of 31 hunger-striking workers, except for Hong Jiaben and others who were sent to the hospital earlier due to severe illness, were forcibly sent to the Labor Hospital and Shanghai Hospital by personnel from the Party and government organs the day before yesterday to prevent their lives from being endangered. A reporter from the Ta Kung Pao specially went to the Labor Hospital yesterday to inquire about the current situation of the workers. According to the nurses in the hospital, after the workers were admitted to the hospital, the doctors examined them separately and recorded their pulse and temperature. They were advised to eat, but the workers still refused to accept. The doctors then gave them medicine, and they were generally fine. However, some people had more serious illnesses, and their symptoms were as follows: Hong Jiaben and Lu Shiying had severe headaches; Hou Zhangyuan and Liu Yuanxing had numbness in their hands and feet; Sun Yucheng had abdominal pain and vomiting; Zhang Zegang had chest pain and nosebleeds.

Families Came to Shanghai to Visit After hearing the news of the hunger strike, the family of hunger-striking worker Sun Handong rushed to Shanghai from their hometown yesterday. They went to the Labor Hospital to visit him. When they saw his pale and thin face and weak spirit, they could not help but burst into tears. Fortunately, Wang Xianqing, a representative of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, and the doctors repeatedly comforted them, and they hired a car to send him to his relatives behind the Great World for temporary accommodation. The family of Zhu Jinsheng also came to Shanghai from their hometown yesterday and went to the Shanghai Hospital to visit his condition, which was very miserable.

Ninth Period of Food Not Received The workers' temporary food maintenance fee is 120 yuan per day, which was originally scheduled to be collected every Wednesday. Except for the previous period's food expenses, which had already been received the day before (Monday), yesterday was the date to receive the ninth period's food expenses. The union representatives Xia Zhongzhao and Qin Haiyan, together with Zhu Guilin, a representative of the Social Affairs Bureau, went to the head office on Nanjing Road yesterday morning to collect the money. They met with Wang Xianhua, a director of the company, who said that the company had decided not to issue the food expenses anymore, so he could not issue them without authorization. He had to ask the board of directors, and it might be issued on Friday (tomorrow). The representatives then left. Refutation of the Board of Directors' Announcement The Wang Association of the Cotton Weaving Industry in the Seventh District believed that the announcement published by the factory's board of directors in various newspapers was inconsistent with the facts. Yesterday, they specially wrote a refutation as follows: Regarding the announcement of the board of directors of Sanyou Industrial Company, we are unwilling to make any more meaningless disputes. Now, we are afraid that people in society will be deceived, so we solemnly declare again to clarify the truth. (1) When the January 28th Shanghai Incident suddenly occurred, the situation was tense, and the capitalists notified the suspension of work the next day to avoid the danger at that time. At that time, the workers' savings were not settled and paid. After the ceasefire agreement was signed, the workers came to collect them one after another. Because the Japanese army had not yet withdrawn from the factory, they repeatedly requested that relief be given before work resumed. The capitalists refused, and the workers had no choice but to pay all the savings successively. However, as of recently, it is feared that there are still a few workers who have not received them. (2) On May 31st, the Japanese army left the factory, and the union first sent a letter to the police of the Fourth Police Station in the Fifth District to protect the factory. On June 2nd, they entered the factory and stayed there, entering from the side door on the west side. At that time, Shen Xiangji had carpenters working there, repairing the factory, not breaking in through the screen. (3) The company has had huge profits over the years. After the ceasefire agreement was signed and the Japanese army had just withdrawn, the company sent people to transport the machines in the factory to the Hangzhou branch, intending to stop the main factory and expand the Hangzhou factory. In short, the capitalists are fabricating facts everywhere to destroy the old workers. Therefore, contradictory words have emerged one after another. Now that the government is arbitrating according to law, it will not be difficult to get to the bottom of the matter. In the future, we will ignore the company's meaningless disputes. (4) Furthermore, the company started with a capital of 500 yuan and has achieved today's results. The profits over the years are in the tens of thousands. Even in the past year, the company's account report showed a profit of more than 320,000 yuan. As for the number of debts, it has not exceeded the number of previous years. The reason for the delay in resuming work is that they deliberately make things difficult. Looking at the recent sudden fire in the factory, the electrical outage, and the closing of the water supply (according to the Bureau of Public Works' statement yesterday, the coppersmith falsely claimed to be acting on the order of the fire brigade, and the Bureau of Public Works has denied this, so who is the instigator? It should not be difficult to find out), we can see a glimpse of the capitalists' intentions. In short, all the workers of our Sanyou Factory are crying out and appealing for a living, and in order to maintain national goods, they are unwilling to implement a violent destruction policy, and they are resorting to passive hunger strikes. The purity of their actions and the sadness of their hearts can be understood by the people of society. If the factory still has a sense of benevolence, for the sake of the suffering of our workers and for the future of the national industry, it should quickly plan to resume work. Then all our workers will naturally, based on the spirit of labor-capital cooperation in the past, voluntarily reduce wages and step up production to assist the development of the national goods industry.

The Union's Comfort The Aid Committee of the General Labor Union for the Hunger-Striking Workers of Sanyou Factory specially sent two members, Ye Xianggao and Shao Xubai, to the hospital yesterday to comfort the hunger-striking workers and told them that the municipal government had submitted the dispute to arbitration and that there would be a considerable solution soon. Please ask the workers to eat first to avoid accidents. The hunger-striking workers listened and nodded to express their gratitude, but they still refused to resume eating.

Completion of Chinese Military Musical Instruments 143

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce, in order to consolidate national spirit and develop national patriotism, initiated Chinese military music at the beginning of last month. The Chamber's Boy Scouts serve as the orchestra, and Zheng Jinwen and Xu Ruhui of the Datong Music Association are invited to plan everything and guide the compilation and training. They first practice short flute and cymbal songs for a month to establish a foundation, and at the same time manufacture musical instruments related to military music in the past dynasties, totaling 34 kinds and 64 pieces. They are all products with loud volume and beautiful timbre, and their strange shapes are rarely seen in modern society. The range of sound is large, from the lowest to the highest, with a total of eight levels. They were completely completed yesterday and handed over to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, which distributed them to the group for distribution and practice. Everyone was overjoyed and indescribable. There are currently about 70 people taking classes on a regular basis, and it is said that there are still a large number of people who continue to join the group. The quota is 100 people, and they are working hard to practice. They plan to perform an outdoor trip on the Double Ten Festival this year as a large-scale promotion.

Chinese Harmonica Association Continues to Run National Crisis Class 145

One-Third of Membership Fees Donated to the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army

The Chinese Harmonica Association aims to study harmonica music, promote noble art, and promote national spirit. Since September 18th last year, although the association has been affected by the current situation, it has still actively carried out various national salvation works. Last year, at the association's first anniversary music conference, it played "Black Horse Galloping" and other pieces to donate to General Ma and various provinces for disaster relief. During the Shanghai War, the association specially compiled "Song of the 19th Route Army" and organized a harmonica team to go to various wounded soldiers' hospitals and the front lines of Su Kun and other places to perform and comfort our loyal and brave soldiers who defended the country. The association also added a "National Crisis Harmonica Class" to teach patriotic and heroic songs to encourage the morale of compatriots and jointly face the national crisis. The results were excellent and were highly praised by the general public. Recently, Chairman Wang of the association, in view of the brave and good fighting of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army for the country, specially compiled "Rising Up to Save the Country" and "March of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army" and other songs to commemorate them. The association continued to set up a "National Crisis Class" at the association's office at 168 Sichuan Road. The time has been set. The evening class is from 7:30 p.m. to 9:00 p.m. every Saturday night, and the day class is from 3:30 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. every Saturday afternoon. The course will be completed in two months. The membership fee is 3 yuan per month per person, of which 1 yuan will be donated to the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army. Mr. Lin Kanghou, a member of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army Support Association, has been invited to supervise the class. Both classes are personally instructed by Chairman Wang. Those who are patriotic and want to study noble harmonica music, regardless of gender or qualifications, please register with the association as soon as possible. The class will start on September 3rd. A booklet is available for filing. In addition, the association's harmonica team is now planning to recruit dozens of new members for expansion. Regardless of whether they are members of the association, those who have a considerable level of proficiency will be added to the research immediately after passing the guidance and review.

Verdict on the Assassination of Wen Ying 146

Fan Hongsheng Sentenced to Fifteen Years of Imprisonment

Fan Hongsheng from Nanjing, also known as Fan Ruibao, had a love affair with female physiognomist Wang Wenying. Because he could not achieve the purpose of marriage, he suspected that Wang's mother, Wu, was obstructing him. He developed evil thoughts and went to Wenying's home at 89 Pingle Lane, Xizang Road at 2 p.m. on July 19th this year with a knife, intending to kill Wang Wu. However, because Wu dodged, he did not hit the vital point and only caused minor injuries. At that time, Wenying saw the situation and shouted loudly. Fan was afraid of being arrested, so he stabbed Wenying several times, all of which hit the vital points, and she died immediately. Fan fled without a trace at that time. He was later arrested by the West Detective of the Lao Zha Police Station at his sister's home on Jiaotong Road, Zhabei. The police station's lawyer, Ru Bao, filed a public prosecution with the First Special Court on the charge of premeditated murder. Fan also hired lawyer Jiang Baoli to defend him, saying that Fan suffered from mental loss and should be exempted from his sentence according to law and requested that he be declared innocent. The Special Court had repeatedly summoned and interrogated the parties,

Page 16

The details have been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Feng Shide, the presiding judge of the Criminal Court, opened the first criminal court and announced the verdict. The main text of the verdict was that Fan Hongsheng was sentenced to 10 years of imprisonment for the crime of murder and 7 years of imprisonment for the crime of attempted premeditated murder, totaling 15 years of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the judgment was determined to be two days for one day of imprisonment. The incidental civil lawsuit was transferred to the Civil Court for trial. Fan's ex-wife (divorced), Yang Xiuying, lived at 2 Shenjia Lane, Sanpailou Road in the city after separating from Fan and worked as a female host at No. 7 at Tianyunlou Amusement Park to make a living.

Longtime Maid Betrays Trust 147

Stealing 2,000 Yuan Worth of Clothing

The Cantonese woman Zhong Wang, who lived at 1099 North Sichuan Road, went to live with relatives on the day after the January 28th incident and asked the maid Qin Yu, a native of Jiangbei, to take care of the house. Unexpectedly, Qin conspired with Zhuang Shilin, a native of Pudong, his wife Wan, and Zhu Dasheng, a native of Yangzhou, to steal all the clothing worth 2,000 yuan and flee without a trace. After Zhong Wang returned home, she reported the theft to the Hongkou Police Station. It was not until the day before yesterday that Detective Sun Aizhong arrested the four suspects and recovered some of the stolen clothes, gold watches, and gold rings. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the first court. Detective Sun Hua reported the circumstances of the arrest of the defendants, and the stolen goods were presented for inspection. The plaintiff, Zhong Wang, stated that she had entrusted the defendant Qin Yu to take care of the house at the time. She did not expect Qin to betray her trust and conspire with the other defendants to move everything out of the house. She had been working for her family for eight years. The items presented in the case were all stolen goods. When questioned, the defendants' confessions were evasive. Judge Shen Bingrong declared to Qin Yu that the mistress trusted her very much because she had been working for her for many years and entrusted her with valuable property. She should not have breached her trust. Qin bowed her head and begged for forgiveness. She was then ordered to be detained separately and the case was scheduled for re-examination.

Ren Jiaping Claims

Ren Jiaping, an old man from Suzhou, dressed like a beggar, went to the District Court yesterday to accuse his son, Ren Lianfang, who currently lives on Guoqing Road, Zhabei. When he was reprimanded, the son heard about it and beat the old man and drove him out of the house, causing him to sleep in the alley in the wind and rain, among the beggars. Bad Luck for Good Fortune Bookstore 153

Selling Obscene Books

Fine of 300 Yuan

The Executive Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters found that the novels "Little White Face", "The Great View of Maritime Mysteries", "New Tide of the Sea of Desire", "Unofficial History of the Meat Forest", "New Tide of Clouds and Rain", "Lu Gaojian", "Spring Colors of the East Neighbor", and "The Flowery Hell" published by the Good Fortune Bookstore at 103 Jiaotong Road, International Settlement, all contained obscene language. There was also a book titled "White River Military Parade Photography," which involved reactionary and pro-Japanese propaganda. The committee sent a letter to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation. Director Wen of the Public Security Bureau forwarded the letter to the Police Department of the Bureau of Public Works and requested the First Special Court to issue a search warrant. The warrant was issued to Chief Patrolman Pang Jinshan and Public Security Bureau investigators, who went to search the bookstore the day before yesterday. Except for the book "White River Military Parade," which was not found, they seized 482 copies of the remaining books and took the manager, Lu Jiying, a native of Guangdong, back to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special Court. The police station's lawyer, Qian Xunjiu, explained the previous situation and stated that the defendant had not submitted the above books to the Ministry of Interior or the Municipal Party Headquarters for registration. Therefore, he is now prosecuting according to Article 251 of the Criminal Law. Furthermore, the defendant violated the provisions of Article 19 of the Publication Law, so he requested that a heavier punishment be imposed according to Article 35 of the Publication Law. Chief Patrolman Pang then submitted a report on the circumstances of the search and interrogated the defendant. Lawyer Wang Peiyuan defended, saying that although the names of the seized books were close to obscene, the content was completely the opposite. The sole purpose was to expose the dark side of society and persuade others to avoid evil paths. He asked the court to read the preface to understand. Therefore, the defendant did not commit any crime and requested that he be declared innocent. After Judge Liu Yugui verified the confession, he sentenced Lu Jiying to a fine of 300 yuan and confiscated the seized books.

International Trade Bureau Compiles Trade Statistics 161

The International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, in order to facilitate the study of international trade, has specially compiled three types of monthly international trade statistics through its Statistics Department: 1. Monthly statistics on total import and export trade; 2. Monthly statistics on the classification of import and export commodities; and 3. Statistics on the countries of import and export trade. The second type of statistics is based on the customs' monthly statistical reports, which have been reclassified and compiled. The special feature is that import and export commodities are divided into four major categories and one hundred and twenty-four minor categories, so that readers can observe the trends of trade and at the same time speculate on the prosperity or decline of our country's industries. For the convenience of historical research, the classification method is still based on the "China International Trade Statistics for Sixty-Five Years" compiled by Yang of the Academia Sinica, which scientifically divides them into four major categories: food and tobacco, raw materials, semi-finished products, manufactured goods, and miscellaneous items. Yang's compilation covers the period up to 1928. In 1929, Hou Houpei and Lou Yun compiled for one year. Now the bureau has compiled from 1930 onwards, so that the seventy years can be continuously referenced. These three types of statistics are printed separately each month and published regularly. The June issue of this year has already been published. If people from all walks of life need to refer to them, please write directly to the International Trade Bureau on Hankou Road to request them.

Domestically produced products are often shoddy, causing the reputation of domestic products to plummet. Letter 170

Regarding the news item published in your newspaper's news column on the 15th of this month ("Kim Koo Has Been Arrested"), we were shocked to read it. The Korean Kim Koo has not been hiding in Chongming, and the Japanese consulate has not notified the authorities to assist in arresting Kim Koo. Furthermore, no Japanese warship has arrived in Chongming and no marines have landed. The sections reported by your newspaper are not only completely fabricated but also have no impact at all. Since the invasion of Shanghai by the brutal Japanese, the party and government agencies and mass organizations in our county have all been deeply saddened. How could we disregard territorial sovereignty and assist the Japanese bandits? The report in your newspaper is probably a false rumor. However, since it concerns the reputation of the entire county, we are sending this letter to correct it in order to dispel public doubts, and we hope that it will be published. Addressed to the Chief Editor of the Shen Bao. From the Chongming County Public Security Bureau, August 22nd.

Notice to Contributors 171

To All Contributors:

We would like to discuss with you the future direction of improvement for this publication. Before addressing this topic, please accept our sincere gratitude. In the past, this publication has been mistakenly given excessive expectations by readers. This is a result of your affection for this publication and your efforts to assist us. However, in our opinion, this publication must also find ways to transform itself to meet the needs of modern society and new readers, and slightly improve its past direction. Therefore, we have decided to strictly regulate the rules for soliciting contributions from September 1st, opening up a new path for this publication. We hope that you will earnestly contribute to this effort, so that this publication can truly achieve its goal of "improvement," and readers in general will feel a deeper interest and sympathy. This is our wish.

The following are the newly revised rules for contributions:

(1) The material must be short stories rich in modernity, such as realistic social snapshots, family and women's life, youth self-cultivation, random thoughts, casual talks, etc.

(2) Manuscripts must be lively in writing, thorough in understanding, sincere in emotion, and rich in interesting flavor. Those with outdated thoughts and stale facts will not be accepted.

(3) In addition to the title, add a sub-title of one or two sentences, which must be very novel and eye-catching. (4) The number of words per article is strictly limited to 500 words. Please indicate the number of words at the end of the manuscript. (5) Manuscripts can be written in either classical or vernacular Chinese, but must use new punctuation marks. Striking phrases must be circled. (6) This publication welcomes short essays of one or two hundred words that are profound and striking or humorous and interesting; and slogan-style aphorisms of three to five hundred words.

(7) Increased payment for contributions; the standard of payment is based on quality, not quantity.

Starting from Hoover's Tears 172

— Yang Yusheng

1928. Mr. Hoover was elected President of the United States. He entered the palace to take office. Hundreds of thousands of people surrounded him and cheered. He came out to thank them, and then retired and wept. Alas, bearing the heavy trust of the entire country, if he did not strive with tears, how could he be diligent and govern well? These were indeed extraordinary tears, not to be expected from the authorities in China. Therefore, China ultimately remained ungoverned. How regrettable!

Japanese world-class athlete Oda Yokota was eliminated due to illness. Filled with anger, tears streamed down his face. Although it involved a petty family spirit, he was worthy of a hero. These were indeed extraordinary tears, not to be expected from the sports community in China. Therefore, China's sports ultimately remained stagnant. How regrettable!

In the 17th year of the Republic [1928], after the split between Nanjing and Wuhan, a certain central committee member said with emotion, "If the leaders of the party and the country do not gather together and embrace each other in tears, there will be no sincere unity." Alas, the words are still in our ears, and five years have passed. In these five years, the so-called leaders of the party and the country have shown nothing but tragedies of squabbling, resigning, declaring, and going abroad. As a result, the national situation is as precarious as it is today. I have not heard of any expression of weeping with shame, repentance, unity, or resistance to foreign aggression. Moreover, they deceive each other and are divided into four or five factions, still in a state of neither death nor life. It is said that only extraordinary people can shed extraordinary tears. This is indeed an extraordinary matter, not to be expected from the party and national leaders of today. Therefore, the foundation of the party is ultimately insecure, and the country is on the verge of destruction. How regrettable!

Shocking news of Rehe came. People ran and cried. A certain senior official cried while receiving reporters and said, "If I and my son do not love the country, how could things be as they are today?" His words were mournful and heartbreaking. However, if this burst of hot tears could be shed on the Nine-Eighteenth Incident [Mukden Incident] to destroy the home and dedicate oneself to fighting the enemy to the death, would it not shock the world and move the gods?

Distinguishing Traitors 173

— Qing

Hu Lifu is known as a [Han traitor]. He has now been taken to Beijing. Consider the word [jian]. Pronounced [gan]. As in the Tang Yun, Ji Yun, and Yun Hui, it is all [gu han qie], slightly different from [ju han qie]. It should not be read as [jian]. The Shuowen also says it means to violate. The Yu Pian says it means to cause chaos. The Zeng Yun only says it means something that is not in accordance with propriety. The Zuo Zhuan, 13th year of Duke Cheng, says [jian jue wo hao] [to break our good relations]. The Han Shu, Guliezhi, says [shi shen ren ge de qi suo, er bu xiang jian] [to enable gods and men to each get what they should, and not to interfere with each other]. The common saying [bu xiang gan] [not related] means this. However, the Ji Yun also reads it as [ju yan qie], pronounced [jian]. It means private, false, and also not read in the flat tone. The Zhuangzi, Tianyun, says [shang yi zhe qi shi er jun] [There were those who used this to overthrow seventy-two rulers]. The Shiji, History of Qi, says [shang yi yu diao jian Zhou] [They used fishing and angling to undermine Zhou]. It is used interchangeably with [gan], and is different from the current meaning of [Han traitor]. Therefore, is the word [jian] in [Han traitor] an error? Consider the fact that [jian] and [jian] have the same pronunciation. The Shuowen says it means private, one saying is fraud or licentiousness. The Book of Documents, Shun Dian, says [kou zei jian gui] [robbers, bandits, traitors, and secret agents]. The commentary says [to rob people is called kou, to kill people is called zei, those outside are called jian, those inside are called gui]. The Li Xue Li says [zheng yi yi qi xing, xing yi fang qi jian] [governance unifies their actions, punishment prevents their treacherous actions]. The Guanzi, Junchen Jie, says [zhi zha ju jian, hou guo zhi dao ye] [to stop fraud and restrain treacherous actions is the way to enrich the country]. [Jian] and [jian] seem the same but are actually different. Therefore, for the term [Han traitor], [jian] should be used, not [jian]. It is very clear. Ancient texts wrote it as [graph omitted], which is an ideogram. However, Korea, which continues to use Chinese books, uniquely uses [jian] for the word [jian] and [jian] for the word [jian], as seen in the Zheng Zi Tong. Thus, there is a different explanation that cannot be followed. Therefore, I write the Distinguishing Traitors.

Even if, unfortunately, it were to be defeated and destroyed, later generations would mourn his ambition and pity his fate. Although these tears have their master, they do not have their time. How regrettable!

Supplementary Record of the Little History of the Flying Eagle 174

— Jing

The Free Talk previously carried a section on the Little History of the Flying Eagle recorded by Jue Min. According to what I know, there are some discrepancies. I would like to correct them.

The Flying Eagle is the only remaining destroyer in our country, currently valued at more than 2 million yuan. Its sailing speed is known to be the highest among naval vessels, approximately 23 nautical miles per hour or more. As Jue Min said, the Empress Dowager Cixi of the late Qing Dynasty once sent it to pursue Kang Youwei, a leading figure in the Hundred Days' Reform, but without success. The ship's boiler was damaged due to overuse during this mission. In the sixth year of the Republic [1917], Chief of Staff Cheng Biguang led the southern expedition to protect the constitution against Yuan Shikai, stationed in the Pearl River, and it was completely abandoned. It was not until Di Jishen governed Guangdong, fearing the emptiness of coastal defense, that he spent 100,000 yuan to repair it. The repairs were for the entire boiler water pipes and some steel plates and machine parts at the bottom of the ship, not the boiler, and certainly not purchased and donated by Borodin. The successive captains from the twelfth to the seventeenth year of the Republic [1923-1928] were Huang Zhen from Jiangxi, followed by Shu Zongliu from Guangdong, who was the leader of the naval resistance against Chen Ce, who occupied the White Goose Pool and fought against the air force in the eighteenth year. Then came Chen Ding, and then Chen Jie, until the current battle when it sank, with Ren Yaokui, who was also the Deputy Adjutant of the Maritime Department. In the middle, there was no change of captain to a Russian, and it was never a stronghold for communist activities. This time, it sank off the coast of Hainan Island. Most newspapers believed it was caused by bombing. In fact, it was not. Although it had been hit by a bullet fired by Ding Jixu, a brave general in the civil war, it was damaged on the right side, destroying one cannon. It was not a critical hit. However, the crew feared death and sought to escape. Moreover, they followed the principle of Chen Qingyun, the commander of the Marine Corps, that it is better to sink the ship than to let it be used by the enemy, so defeat is still glorious. Alas, given the weakness of our country's existing navy and the fact that national power is not available for construction, there are people who do not cherish it at all and recklessly demonstrate their martial prowess, destroying national instruments in internecine strife. How regrettable!

The Secret History of the Twenty-One Demands (3) 177

— Si Ping

On February 25th, I went to Beijing. I arrived on February 27th. On February 28th, I visited Minister Reinsch, but did not meet him. On March 1st, I had an important conversation with Reinsch. He told me that he had already forwarded our petition to the American government. He asked me to write to Stone, the director of the Associated Press of America, to visit Chinda, the Japanese ambassador to the United States, and to ask Wang Zhengting and Kong Xiangxi to persuade the Chinese people to remain calm. I also asked Reinsch to see Sir John Jordan, the British ambassador, and strongly pointed out the impropriety of Britain's protection of Japanese atrocities.

I learned from other sources that Hioki Eki intended to directly see Yuan Shikai with the Twenty-One Demands. He took out the articles and read them to Yuan one by one. President Yuan then asked him if he had already submitted these demands to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Hioki Eki replied that he had not gone to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and came directly to see the President. Yuan Shikai told him that China was a constitutional country, and these demands must be submitted to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. However, Hioki Eki turned a deaf ear, insisted on leaving the articles of demand on the table, and left. Yuan Shikai then summoned Sir John Jordan and Reinsch to study the matter.

Before the Twenty-One Demands were presented, Hioki Eki invited Moore, a reporter from the Associated Press of America, and J.O.P. Bland, a reporter from The Times of London, in advance. Hioki Eki said to them, "The Japanese government is holding a grand event at this time, and we invite you to go. All travel expenses will naturally be covered by the Japanese government. You can take this opportunity to go to Japan for sightseeing. You can gain a deeper understanding of Japan." Enticed by these sweet words, they accepted the invitation and went to Tokyo. Their duties in Beijing were taken over by their assistants.

As soon as these two important journalists left Beijing, Hioki Eki hurriedly presented the demands to Yuan Shikai. The next morning, the British embassy telephoned the Beijing reporters of The Times of London and the Associated Press of America, Moore and J.O.P. Bland, asking them to come. Unfortunately, they had already been tricked into going to Tokyo by Hioki Eki's ruse. The assistants of Moore and J.O.P. Bland went to the British embassy. The British embassy gave them each a copy of the Twenty-One Demands, instructing them to telegraph them to The Times of London and the Associated Press of America for publication. Stone, the director of the Associated Press of America, received the telegram of the Twenty-One Demands and found it very strange. He did not dare to publish it. Stone took the telegraphic manuscript to see Chinda, the Japanese ambassador to Washington, requesting confirmation. Chinda vehemently denied it. Later, the Japanese government also formally denied it. Stone then telegraphed Moore, severely reprimanding him for not distinguishing between truth and falsehood and sending a telegram of the Twenty-One Demands, which was enough to provoke war, and ordered an investigation into the source of the news. The Times of London also sent a similar telegram to J.O.P. Bland.
